This Old French term "de litargie" refers to the ancient practice of bloodletting—a common medical treatment during medieval times thought by some practitioners to cure or prevent illnesses by removing bad humors from a patient's body, particularly in cases where it was believed that an imbalance existed within. The term "litargie" derives from the Greek word "leitis," meaning "to bleed." Bloodletting could be performed using various tools, including lancets or cauteries (burning instruments), depending on the method and severity of treatment desired by the physician.
